Bond Prices Fell Sharply Last Week 131

Down by About 2-3 Yuan from the Previous Week

Transactions Exceeded 13.8 Million

Last week, the bond market situation at the Shanghai Securities Exchange saw continuous scarcity in spot transactions, with only 38,000 yuan traded throughout the week. The futures market was extremely lively, with each of Monday and Wednesday seeing 18-19 million traded, and Tuesday, Thursday, and the weekend seeing 23-24 million each. Friday saw the highest volume, with nearly 30 million yuan traded in a single day. Total transactions for the week reached 13,876,000 yuan. The most active trading was in the China Consolidated Tax 2.0 bonds. Consolidated tax bonds accounted for 27,495,000 yuan for September and 10,745,000 yuan for October. China Consolidated Tax 2.0 bonds accounted for 23,035,000 yuan for September and 6,780,000 yuan for October. The salt tax market was also very active, accounting for 24,470,000 yuan, with 18,895,000 yuan for September and 5,575,000 yuan for October. Other bonds also outperformed, such as China Consolidated 2.0 bonds, accounting for 10,795,000 yuan for September and 2,935,000 yuan for October. The demobilization bonds accounted for 6,595,000 yuan for September and 3,480,000 yuan for October. The 1.9 customs bonds totaled 7,860,000, the 1.9 reconstruction bonds totaled 6,295,000 yuan, the reorganization bonds totaled 6,035,000 yuan, the 9.6 public bonds totaled 1,045,000 yuan, and the fully consolidated customs tariffs totaled 580,000 yuan. There was also 10,000 yuan for 1918 bonds and 25,000 yuan for financial bonds. Total transaction volume exceeded the previous week by over 57.3 million yuan. Regarding the price movements of various bonds within the past week, due to the issuance of new bonds, supply exceeded demand in the market. Furthermore, with the vast national disaster areas this time, there were concerns that future tax revenues would decrease, and rumors of military actions frequently spread, causing unease in the market. Sellers were eager to sell, and speculative selling was also active. Selling pressure dominated the market, and bond prices uniformly fell sharply under this pressure, falling by 1-2 yuan on Monday. On Tuesday, they fell by a small 0.5-0.6 yuan to 1 yuan and several jiao. Wednesday and Thursday each fell by about 1 yuan, with a very strong continuous decline, causing considerable tension in the market. However, on Friday, there was a sudden and significant rebound, as short-sellers covered their profits and the market took advantage of the low prices to invest. The strength of the rebound far exceeded the previous decline. On this day, bonds such as the China Consolidated 2.0 and salt tax bonds jumped by over 3 yuan, and others also rose by about 2 yuan. However, sentiment turned negative again on the weekend, and prices weakened, resulting in a net decrease of 2-3 yuan compared to the previous week. Only the 9.6 1918 bonds had no major fluctuations. Looking at the bond market situation, it is expected to gradually return to stability in the short term. Yarn and Cotton – Yarn Market Listless Last Week 132

Actual Sales Extremely Sluggish

The yarn market last week showed no signs of glory or disgrace. The market situation was extremely listless. Due to the base price, there were fewer new sellers. However, the overall situation was very bad. There were many rumors about the current situation, which did not affect sentiment much, and it was entirely due to the overestimation of the base price. Furthermore, the large players had not given up the idea of selling short. A certain large merchant once again lost money by covering a short position. A certain Japanese trading firm viewed the severity of the Chinese floods and feared that actual sales would be greatly affected in the future. Therefore, they were extremely bearish and sold off a significant amount, putting a lot of pressure on the market. As for the large Chinese merchants, their attitude remained negative, but there were fewer vigorous sellers, so they maintained a firm stance this week. The US cotton situation was very soft on the weekend, but the price of third-grade yarn tended to rise, causing profit-takers to cover short positions, and the market rose. As a result, the price of benchmark yarn for each month rose by one or two taels compared to the previous week. The sales of spot yarn among customer firms became even more sluggish. There was no large-scale activity from any party. Japanese firms issued a significant amount of forward yarn, and the prices were relatively low, all of which were accepted by Japanese trading firms. The future of the yarn market is still uncertain. However, the world cotton industry situation is still in a state of despair.

Cotton Market Hovering Last Week 133

New Cotton Arriving in Abundance

The cotton market has been in a state of flux for a week, but the overall situation is very dangerous. The second estimate of the world surplus of American cotton showed an increase in production of over 100,000 bales. Fortunately, prices were temporarily maintained and did not fall. However, Japanese merchants purchased cheap Indian cotton and sold benchmark cotton, which slightly affected the market. Local cotton was damaged by floods from various routes, and the annual yield was greatly reduced. Therefore, most cotton merchants were in a long position, holding tight and not releasing. However, most people viewed the foreign surplus and vigorously sold short. Traders showed little interest in spot cotton transactions. However, the long and short sides held their positions more and more forcefully. The price of benchmark cotton for each month was similar to the previous week. New cotton was arriving in abundance. American cotton fell by 5 pounds compared to the previous week, according to reports.

American Cotton Falls, British and Indian Cotton Rise Slightly 134

Yesterday, American cotton was weak due to a lack of major buyers, good weather, and Southern hedging sales. Futures fell by 7-11 points, and spot prices fell by 10 points. British cotton futures rose 2-3 points, and spot prices rose 3 points. Egyptian cotton spot prices were unchanged. Indian cotton short sellers covered their positions, and the market was firm. The price of Pingguoer rose by 1.5 rupees, Aomula rose by 1.75 rupees, and Bailuoxi rose by 2 rupees, according to original telegrams (dated the 12th).

Silk and Tea – Wuxi Autumn Silk Prices Rise Sharply 137

Cocoon Shops Release Prices to Compete for Purchases…Cocoon Prices Rise to 100 Yuan

The autumn silkworm rearing in the four rural districts of Wuxi is quite active. Unfortunately, the most important period of dormancy was plagued by wind and rain, followed by major floods. Mulberry fields were submerged, resulting in a shortage of raw materials, and cocoon prices rose surprisingly. Each dan required about 4 yuan. The silkworms were damaged by cold rain, and diseases such as white spots were discovered. Early silkworm cocoons have already entered the market, and late silkworms have also been caged. It is estimated that cocoon production will be no more than 60%. Cocoon shops in various districts have been releasing prices to compete for purchases, and cocoon prices have been rising. The northeast district is the highest, with high-quality foreign variety cocoons already reaching 100 yuan. The southwest districts are also at 85-90 yuan. It is expected that prices will continue to rise in the future, it was said.

Metals – New Lead Wire Price Drops by 1 Qian and a Half 138

Yesterday was Sunday, and metal transactions were even scarcer as a result. There were few general goods in the market, and no large-scale transactions could be said to have taken place. However, the price of new lead wire, which has long been in short supply, fell sharply yesterday as there were many sellers and few buyers. The standard price fell by 1 qian and a half, selling for 13 taels (Nos. 16-20). As for Nos. 21-25, each dan was only valued at 18 taels and 5 qian. According to yesterday's market opening, there were only 300-400 dan. In addition, various iron shops saw only minor amounts of incoming and outgoing goods, so there were no gains or losses, it was said.

Black Iron Sheets – Over 2,000 Dan Arrived Yesterday 139

According to news from the tea association, 18 sheets of scarce spot black iron sheets, weighing 2,300-2,400 dan, arrived at the New Taikoo Warehouse yesterday. It is feared that the local market will no longer have to worry about a shortage of goods in the future.

Kong Xiangxi Responds to Wu Tiecheng's Telegram 149

Kong Xiangxi replied to Wu Tiecheng, saying: Urgent, Brother Wu Tiecheng, Committee Member, Beiping, respectful greetings. Secret. Yue Jun forwarded the grey telegram, which was received. The three gentlemen wept bitterly and presented their words, hoping to recover the nation's fortunes. These words of wisdom are widely beneficial. I deeply admire and comfort you. There should be no shortage of patriots in Guangdong. Reading it will surely cause them to awaken suddenly. If they can abandon their suspicions and resentments, and rein in their horses and turn their spears, the survival of the party and the nation depends on this. I am determined for peace, but I am ashamed of my weak power. I am delighted to hear of your esteemed telegram, which truly resonates with my heart. If there is a reply from the Guangdong side, I eagerly await to be informed. Please convey my humble sentiments to the two gentlemen, Shi and Pu. Respectfully, Kong Xiangxi bows. Text.

Song Ziwen Returned to Nanjing Last Night 150

Before leaving, he convened Zhu Qinglan and others for discussions.

Public Announcement by the Disaster Relief Committee Regarding Funds Received Before and After

More than 2 million silver dollars, over 70,000 taels of silver.

Mr. Song Ziwen, Chairman of the National Government's Flood Relief Committee, after convening a plenary meeting of the Flood Relief Committee during his last visit to Shanghai, also convened a meeting of the Standing Committee the day before yesterday, deciding on methods for transporting American wheat and other items. It is now learned that Mr. Song, due to the importance of financial affairs, took the Shanghai night express train back to Nanjing at 11:45 last night to attend to his duties, and is expected to come to Shanghai again next Wednesday or Thursday to handle disaster relief matters. Mr. Song also convened Zhu Qinglan, a standing committee member of the association, and other committee members for discussions before leaving Shanghai at 10:00 yesterday morning. The discussions lasted for about an hour before they dispersed.

▲ Financial Group Announces Funds Received. The Financial Group of the Disaster Relief Committee issued another announcement yesterday, expressing gratitude for the second round of generous donations from all sectors at home and abroad, totaling 1,489,649.49 yuan, 2,891.00 small silver dollars. The total funds received before and after amounted to 2,534,224.55 silver dollars, 2,935.00 small silver dollars, and 3,318 copper coins. The second round also received 11,531.79 taels of silver, bringing the total amount of silver received before and after to 73,316.70 taels.

▲ Li and Bei, Two Committee Members, Travel to Hankou. Mr. Li Jin, a committee member of the Hankou Branch of the National Government's Flood Relief Committee, returned to Hankou by China National Aviation Corporation plane yesterday morning at 7:00 after reporting in Shanghai on his last flight. Mr. Baker, a foreign committee member of the association, is scheduled to go to Hankou to work tomorrow (Tuesday).

Disaster Relief News from Various Provinces Yesterday 151

Starting to Centralize the Accommodation of Disaster Victims

▲ Disaster Victims Arrive Unceasingly. The number of disaster victims arriving from Jiangbei and Jiujiang has been increasing in recent days. The night before last, there were seven or eight hundred people by train, and yesterday there were two or three hundred people arriving from Jiujiang. Today, Taikoo's ship is also bringing more, arriving continuously. The city's disaster relief office had not received prior notice, and the sudden arrival of disaster victims, coupled with the scarcity of personnel, made the handling quite difficult. As of yesterday morning, the number of people accommodated had reached more than 1,700. After arriving in Shanghai, most of the Jiangbei disaster victims sought out relatives and friends and scattered in all directions. Even if they wanted to be accommodated, they were unwilling. However, those who could not find relatives and friends were left wandering on the streets, begging for food and money.

▲ Preparations Before Centralization. The disaster relief office invited the heads of various departments and groups yesterday to discuss distribution methods, deciding that at 5:30 today, each department and group would gather at the office, first transporting the disaster victims from the Chaozhou Wuyi Mountain Villa in batches to the first shelter on Liuying Road, then transporting the disaster victims from the Dawang Temple and Yongxi Hall Zhejiang Shaoxing Association, followed by the Qu Zhenren Temple, and then the Chaozhou Hui Mountain Villa disaster victims. This time, the disaster victims were all picked up and transported by China Moving and Transportation Automobile Company at any time, free of charge. As soon as the disaster victims arrived in Shanghai, they were spared the hardship of trekking. For the convenience of the office, Xiang Sheng Automobile Company dispatched a car every day for the office's use, and their enthusiasm was unparalleled.

▲ Facilities After Centralization. In addition to the office and other sheds, the first shelter on Liuying Road currently has 170 rooms available for accommodation, which can accommodate about 1,700 people. Another 230 rooms are under construction, and when fully completed, it can accommodate 4,000 people. Centralization has now begun, and the interior is being tidied and arranged, with much activity. It is planned to receive visitors from all walks of life after a bit of progress has been made. Since the disaster victims come from inland, in addition to Western medical treatment, traditional Chinese medicine treatment is added. The Traditional Chinese Medicine Association has sent personnel to take charge, and 50 beds have also been set up.

▲ Refusal of Alms and Money. The people of this city are happy to provide relief. Since the arrival of the disaster victims in Shanghai, in order to fulfill their purpose of direct giving, they have been giving money, bread, and biscuits to the temporary shelters. At most, each person could receive 1.45 yuan a day. Therefore, there were people who did not know how to be content and deliberately cried out in distress, hoping to enjoy the benefits of charity continuously, causing various difficulties in the management and disposal of the shelter, which was deeply troublesome. A notice was issued to all sectors a few days ago, stating: "Respectfully inform all benefactors that out of compassion for the disaster victims arriving in Shanghai, they have unanimously made the great wish to provide relief, and have directly given to various shelters without consulting this office. Their kindness and compassion are deeply admired. However, the disaster victims come from all directions, and their customs differ. Wandering people are inevitable. We are deeply concerned that the constant stream of charity may arouse the hearts of those who are greedy and opportunistic, or incite them to surround the donors, causing shouts, robberies, and dangers that are difficult to overcome. This office should do its best to protect the disaster victims, and any deficiencies are due to the limitations of the situation. In an instant, the sheds of the first shelter will be completed and centralized accommodation will be realized. We hereby publish this notice to inform all kind-hearted people that in the future, if there are any donations for the disaster victims arriving in Shanghai, whether they are clothes or money, we would be very grateful. However, we hope that the type and quantity of items can be informed to this office in advance, and after negotiating the distribution methods, this office will arrange to do it together on a regular basis to avoid accidents and effectively benefit the disaster victims. Regarding the flour, bread, biscuits, and other items donated by all sectors, since we have already prepared our own supplies, they have been set aside for a while and are easily moldy, and we are especially afraid of wasting them, which would defeat the intention of the gift. If you could give us clothing, blankets, or practical and durable items, the disaster victims would be even more grateful. We respectfully request your consideration, all gentlemen."

▲ Traditional Chinese Medicine Association Serves the Nation. The Traditional Chinese Medicine Association organized two medical teams for disaster victims to serve in the shelters. Later, the office of the shelter sent a letter stating that the disaster victims had gradually gathered in the shelter on Liuying Road, and a Chinese medicine department had been set up inside, requesting them to come to serve. The association reorganized the medical team, and the director of the secretariat, Jiang Wenfang, convened a meeting late into the night, deciding to hire Shi Xingliu and Shao Chunqiao as resident doctors, and Shu as a resident staff member, lodging in the shelter. The volunteer doctors were divided into six groups and dispatched to work in shifts. Various forms were prepared and printed for recording each patient, daily treatment, classification reports, doctor attendance reports, and weekly medical reports. This afternoon at 2:00, all the doctors will depart from the association.

▲ The Salvation Army Undertakes Relief Work in Xinghua. According to the Zi Lin Daily, after the National Government's Flood Relief Committee requested the Salvation Army to undertake relief work in the Xinghua area of Jiangbei, Major Shan Song, the general secretary of the army, and Captain Shi Delan, a staff member, came to Shanghai from Beiping to discuss everything with the Flood Relief Committee. Currently, the disaster situation in Xinghua is becoming more severe, and the water level is almost equal to the city wall. They will rush to the disaster area within a few days to carry out relief. Other staff members of the army have also departed from North China and are heading south. Currently, the relief expenses are borne by the army, and 12,000 yuan has been deposited in HSBC to open a disaster relief account. It is hoped that after soliciting relief from the British and American Salvation Army, a large amount of money can be raised to continuously supply the disaster area. In addition to providing emergency relief, the army will also conduct a detailed survey of the disaster situation in the four townships so that they can provide relief to the affected farmers in the villages as soon as they receive supplies. It is also hoped that a large amount of American wheat can be allocated to be distributed in the county. The salaries and expenses of the relief workers will be paid separately by the army and will not be used for relief funds.

Record of the Yangzhou Association Meeting 152

The Yangzhou Eight Counties Shanghai Fellow Association convened a meeting again yesterday afternoon at 2:00 to address the urgent relief of the Jiangbei flood. The committee members Shen Dingchen, Li Zhixi, Ruan Mubai, Jiao Dingkai, Xu Fuchen, Zhu Jiuqing, Zhou Yinting, Song Shi, Qian Shusheng, Shi Hanzhang, Chen Yangfu, Cheng Shuzhi, Zhou Yaoting, and over a hundred others attended. Shen Dingchen chaired the meeting, followed by Jiao Dingkai representing the chairman, reporting on the progress of the urgent relief. Then, Committee Member Ruan Mubai introduced Wang Jingting, the chairman of the Yangzhou General Chamber of Commerce, who reported on the disaster situation in Yangzhou. The association immediately pledged 2,000 yuan to be handed over to Chairman Wang to be distributed in Yangzhou, while continuing to raise funds. Committee Member Jiao Dingkai was appointed to attend the National Government's Flood Relief Committee in Nanjing.

Report on the Work of the Jiangsu Flood Relief Association's Various Offices 153

▲ Mr. Zhu Qiliu from the Gaoyou office of the Jiangsu Flood Relief Association reported: Upon my arrival in Gaoyou under orders, I organized an office to engage in temporary relief efforts. However, the Gaoyou dike had breached for over two "li" (approximately 0.6 miles), with surging waves and a sound like thunder. Except for the section at the Pipa Gate south of the city, the area was a vast expanse of water, a veritable swamp. Day after day, refugees flocked in, overwhelming our capacity to accommodate them. They ate in the wind and slept in the dew, a truly miserable sight. They wandered along the dike, everywhere. I was heartbroken and deeply anxious upon witnessing this. I respectfully submit this report detailing our adherence to the agreed-upon relief methods, the current state of our work, and our future plans, for your kind perusal.

A. Past Work Situation:

(1) Regarding Rescue Operations: We have requested 40 civilian boats from the Gaoyou Flood Relief Society. When this number is insufficient, we will hire additional boats from this office to go to various villages to conduct rescue operations. Each boat rescues approximately one thousand refugees. After the rescue, they are temporarily sent to shelters. Those who volunteer to go south are sent off accordingly.

(2) Regarding Accommodation:

a. Shelters: Gaoyou City is submerged in several feet of water, with no dry land to be found. Currently, only the Great King Temple can be used as a shelter. We have temporarily established the First Shelter there. The shelter accommodates over 4,000 refugees daily. Some stay for one night before being sent south, while others remain there permanently. They receive two meals a day, and the order is generally good. The Jieshou branch has established a shelter at Yongxing Temple, accommodating over 400 refugees daily. The situation is largely the same as in Gaoyou.

b. Sending Away: The local authorities are currently arranging for boat transportation. Sailing begins at 8:00 AM daily, with four tugboats transporting over 1,500 refugees each day. If local financial resources are insufficient in the future, this office will subsidize coal to assist with the relief efforts.

(3) Regarding Soup Kitchens: The city is submerged in several feet of water, and the number of disaster victims is far greater than outside the city. This is because other charitable organizations are providing temporary relief outside the city, while traffic in the city is cut off, and there are fewer rescuers. Therefore, we first established a soup kitchen at Yongqing Temple in the city. We have already begun investigating, and it will be opened as soon as the investigation is completed. Most of the disaster victims outside the city have gathered at the Taishan Temple, Chengtian Temple, and Tianwang Temple, and the Gaoyou Flood Relief Society is responsible for providing food for them. Disaster victims who have not entered these three places are all registered and released by the First Soup Kitchen at Yongqing Temple in the city.

(4) Regarding Burial: After the river dike collapsed, floating corpses drift with the waves. We have hired staff and boats to search for them. However, they are scattered by the冲激 and even the corpses that have been found have no place to bury them. We are urgently seeking high ground and trying to bury them.

(5) Regarding Epidemic Prevention: We have hired local Chinese and Western doctors to set up an epidemic prevention hospital to carry out prevention.

(6) Regarding Livestock Protection: Disaster victims are everywhere and difficult to accommodate, so livestock protection can only be considered later.

B. Future Work Plan:

(1) Regarding Rescue Operations: For disaster victims in remote and impoverished areas who stubbornly cling to their homeland and refuse to move elsewhere, the Jisheng Society is now providing relief in Gaoyou. We plan to consult with them and ask them to take on the relief efforts.

(2) Regarding Accommodation:

a. Accommodation: The shelters here are already overcrowded. We do not know how many more people can be accommodated in the shelters in the provinces of Shanghai and Yangzhou. We plan to investigate in detail to allocate and send them.

b. Sending Away: Gaoyou City is entirely submerged in water, and the number of refugees rescued is very large and cannot be accommodated. We plan to set up a temporary transit camp elsewhere as a temporary shelter for refugees going south, providing two meals a day and sending them south the next day.

c. Regarding Soup Kitchens: After the Yongqing Temple soup kitchen is established, if refugees are crowded, we plan to add another one to spread.

d. Regarding Burial: We plan to hire staff and hire more boats to go to the surrounding villages to search for corpses and choose more high ground to bury them to avoid causing an epidemic.

e. Regarding Epidemic Prevention: Please note that all shelters should pay attention to the cleanliness of refugees and take preventive measures. However, it is in deep autumn, and the general disaster victims have not yet stopped crying from hunger, and they will be cold again. The days ahead are long, how can we continue? We urge you to quickly prepare clothing, various medicines for autumn epidemics, and a large amount of relief funds and food to ensure that the disaster victims who did not die in the water can preserve a line of life. I am eager to await orders.

▲ Baoying

(1) Rescue Team: This team hired relief friends to set off in different ways, rescue the disaster victims and went ashore. There have been seven times. The first time was by Zhu Zhongxiang, Zhang Cixu, Shi Yangli, and other gentlemen, each leading ships to Jushi Fan's house, Dongxi Louzitou, Bantudi, Wangjia Village, Xujiawei, Xiaoxingoukou, etc. The second time was by Tian Youzhi, Wu Chunqing, and other gentlemen, leading ships to the Shanbaodi area. The third time was by Fan Dihou, Cheng Aiquan, Lu Qibo, Guo Guizhi, Jia Zuoxian, and other gentlemen, each leading ships to the area along Taipingdi to Shanbaodi. The fourth time was by Tong Yishan, Hu Yangwu, Zhu Xue, and other gentlemen, each leading ships to Minbian Bridge, Sanligou, Kawan, Qiligou, Zhujia Grave, Shanbaodi, Tongledi, Bantudi, Daxiaolujia Village, Lijia Village, Linjia Village, and Hulubridge. The fifth time was by Zhu Haidong, Wang Yichang, Zou Linbo, Zhang Muxu, and other gentlemen, each leading ships to the Wangjia Village area of Shanbaodi. The sixth time was by Wang Runzhi, Zhu Liquan, and other gentlemen, each leading ships to the Dongxiang, Zhujia Village, Zhangjia Village, and other areas. The villages passed along the way were almost the same. The fields and rice paddies were completely submerged, and the houses collapsed, without a complete one. It is difficult to count the scattered farmers, and there are also many deaths. Some live in broken temples, or occupy the top of the roof. All relief friends advance bravely in the midst of狂風巨浪, rescuing disaster victims one after another. According to statistics, more than 3,000 disaster victims have been rescued. Now the seventh batch has set off in three ways. The first route, led by Wei Yuting and Cheng Aiquan, led ships to Baishenanfen, Wagou Qifen, and Jushi Tubi, etc., has not yet returned to the city. The second route, led by Sheng Yunwu and Liu Jinsheng, led ships to Yinhuang蜆松袁卡灣 and other places, and rescued dozens of disaster victims and accommodated them in the second place. The third route, led by Wang Yannong and Zou Linbo, led ships to Sheyang Caoji Tianping狮獍兰亭决溪 and other places, and did not return to the city. They also carried dry food, flour, self-ignition, and various kinds of potion, respectively, to rescue. They are still setting off one after another, and will report again.

(2) Accommodation Team: Before the establishment of this team at this office, they led ships to Gaoyou to rescue disaster victims. Later, the people of Gaoyou were sent to this county one after another. Because of the flood in the west and the rise in the tide, the embankments continued to collapse, and the disaster was severe. The name was changed to accommodate the disaster victims in this county. The first accommodation center was set up in the City God Temple, and the second accommodation center was set up in the Dongyue Temple. The director of supervisors and the cookery officer have been appointed to handle everything. The number of disaster victims who have been accommodated and sent away has reached more than 200. There are more than 100 disaster victims in the first accommodation center, and dozens of disaster victims in the second accommodation center, some of whom are old and weak, or extremely bitter.

(3) Current water situation: The county suffered a severe flood. The west embankment has been submerged for a long time, and the rivers and lakes are connected. Since the collapse of the dam water and the Gaoyou Shao dike, the embankments on the east bank have continued to collapse, the fields have been washed away, and the houses have collapsed. The water depth outside the front door is two or three feet, and boats can pass. The northeast gate surrounds the city, and the ocean is endless. Flood control dams are built outside the city, so the water in the city cannot be discharged. The city river occasionally overflows the shore, and residents and pedestrians feel inconvenient.

▲ Xinghua

Li Rongzhuang from the Xinghua Rescue Team reported: On the 29th of last month, I and my brother Yang Jingshan drove the Jiang Shun and Jiang Su gasoline engines with four tugboats and arrived in Yangzhou at 12:00 midnight. When entering the city, there was no ship available. After inquiring about the water situation up and down the river, I learned that the six-gate water hand gasoline engine could travel. So I hired two lead boatmen and left Yangzhou on the 30th morning. At dusk, I arrived at Fanchuan. There was no shore to moor the boat in the middle of the river. Passing through Qiaoshu, Yangjia Village, Zhenwu Temple, and other places, collapsed houses were everywhere. The low water level reached the eaves. The former streets were all connected to the big river. The broken tiles and ruins were submerged in the shocking waves. Only the branches or treetops of the trees could be seen, floating on the water. I have never seen the main stem. For example, in the old people's village of Taishu, there are still scattered fragments, and the disaster victims are gathered together, depending on each other like cattle and dogs, on a small piece of dry land. It is also miserable. Floating corpses and coffins are everywhere. If the wind and waves are strong, it is difficult to protect the safety of the people living on the embankment. On the 31st morning, I arrived at Laoge, 30 miles away from Xinghua City. I could not find this dangerous embankment. In the waves, I saw a piece of green willow and knew it was a village house. There were faint small boats. There were no houses left. Occasionally, the ones that could be seen had collapsed, or only the roof tiles remained. Arriving at the city, I saw that most of the people's houses in the southwest suburbs were facing the river. The remaining water passed through the windows and doors. The boat was docked in the river outside the South Gate. A small boat was used to cross to the city gate, and then a small boat in the city was used. Except for the county government office building in the city, which was not submerged in water, the water outside the two gates was ankle-deep. The disaster victims who had previously taken refuge in the water were submerged in the water again. Those in the city were shoulder-deep or submerged to the top of their heads, and the shallow ones were submerged to the heels. More than 30 places of the city walls collapsed. On the market, five yuan banknotes could not be exchanged for five yuan in cash. On September 1st, relief friend Mr. Song Zhifang, along with provincial committee members Zhang Baozhen and Li Yuting, scattered emergency relief in the north of the city. A locomotive dragged a Jianghua boat carrying dry food and released it. After traveling five miles to Wujindang, the wind was strong, the waves were surging, and the waves were several feet high. They called for help and floated to Yan's Village, three miles away from the city, and tied the boat to the treetops. At noon on the 2nd, the wind subsided a little before returning to the city. On the 3rd, the wind subsided, and on the 4th, it continued to be released. In this wind disaster, countless houses collapsed in the countryside and the city. All the refugees were loaded and gathered about 2,000 people. The first batch was towed by two gasoline boats and four tugboats, totaling 200 people. They left Xinghua on the morning of the 4th and picked up another 70 refugees in the Yangjia Village area. They arrived in Yangzhou in the evening and were sent to Changsheng Temple outside the Quekou City on the morning of the 5th. The roster was handled by provincial government members Li Yuting and Guo Jifen. Mr. Song Zhifang is still working in Xinghua to organize relief work. The lower river is the most bitter in Xinghua. Those who have not died are still begging for continuous relief.

▲ Regulations on refugee work

The association thought that the number of refugees in each shelter is increasing day by day. They are sitting and eating all day long and doing nothing. In the blink of an eye, the weather is getting cold and cotton clothes are urgently needed. We can't make them in time. Now we have telegraphed to each office to set up sewing work, purchase cloth and cotton nearby, and divide the refugees to sew cold clothes. This can save sewing costs and prevent the disaster victims from sitting idle.

▲ Telegraphing for rice clothes relief funds

The association received a telegram yesterday from the office in Yangzhou, saying that the number of refugees is increasing day by day, please transport hundreds of stones of rice and 3,000 bags of flour. Gaoyou asked for 150 people and 2,000 bags of flour, and 20,000 yuan. Xinghua Baoying also telegraphed to ask for additional funds and rice.

Upstream Yangtze River Anti-Foreign Steamer Movement 158

Organizing a Merchants' Shipping Joint Association

To serve as a backing for the recovery of navigation rights

For years, the Yichang-Chongqing route of the upper Yangtze River has been monopolized by foreign steamers, and Chinese merchant ships have been completely defeated. Now, various organizations in Yichang, seeing the gradual disappearance of Chinese ships and the potential unemployment of over ten thousand workers who rely on the port for their livelihoods, consider this a matter of utmost importance concerning national rights and people's livelihoods. Therefore, they have united labor and capital groups related to shipping to organize a Merchants' Shipping Joint Association, formulate plans, and actively proceed. The following is a record of their correspondence with the Shanghai Chamber of Commerce:

▲Telegram from the Merchants' Shipping Joint Association to the Shanghai Chamber of Commerce: Our country's shipping industry is bound by unequal treaties, having lost both exclusive benefits and the right to protection. Coastal and inland rivers are open to all, foreign ships roam freely, and inland waterways have become foreign ports. This is a rare occurrence in the international community, causing humiliation and loss of national rights like no other. As a result, our country's shipping industry suffers from the economic oppression of imperialists and the destructive force of their violence. Losses of life and property are unbearable, and even tragic incidents occur frequently, which are infuriating. Consequently, Chinese merchant ships are being boycotted by foreign imperialist steamers and are gradually disappearing. Over ten thousand workers who rely on Yichang port for their livelihoods are also facing the threat of unemployment. Although the government has repeatedly issued orders: (1) The Ministry of Industry instructs all provincial organizations to prioritize the use of domestic shipping companies for transporting domestic goods and materials. (2) The National Government instructs all administrative and educational institutions and all public organizations nationwide to use domestic shipping companies for transporting public goods and materials. (3) The Ministry of Finance instructs all customs offices to provide convenience to domestic goods transported by Chinese ships at all times and not to create difficulties. These three measures were circulated to all provinces, cities, and chambers of commerce by the Ministry of Industry and the Ministry of Communications in March of this year. However, due to our country's habitual procrastination, government orders are often mere formalities. Unscrupulous merchants, ignorant of national shame, not only curry favor with foreigners but also obstruct matters from within. Even during this tense anti-Japanese period, they secretly purchase enemy goods and provide them to enemy ships for transportation. Speaking of this is heartbreaking. If this continues, the nation will cease to exist. Recognizing this, the members of this association, bearing the responsibility of every citizen, aim to support Chinese ships and maintain labor livelihoods. Therefore, in accordance with Article 39 of the Provisional Constitution, we have united labor and capital groups related to shipping in Yichang to form this association. We have submitted it to the Party, military, and political authorities for record-keeping. Following Dr. Sun Yat-sen's teachings, complying with government orders, and under the guidance of the Party headquarters, we are formulating plans to adapt to the times, take legal steps, achieve the goal of maintenance, implement our proposals, and strive hard. We are encouraging and formulating plans to adapt to the times, taking legal steps to fully load Chinese ships in order to regain rights and serve as a backing for the government to recover navigation rights, thereby maintaining the livelihoods of laborers. Work began on September 4th. However, at the beginning of this venture, we are facing many challenges. The members of this association have limited strength but heavy responsibilities, and we fear failure. We hope that all of you will show your patriotic enthusiasm and provide assistance to facilitate our progress. This urgent telegram is respectfully submitted for your consideration. Merchants' Shipping Joint Association, Yichang, respectfully. Jiang.

▲Reply telegram from the Shanghai Chamber of Commerce to the Merchants' Shipping Joint Association in Yichang: Your telegram of the Jiang matter has been received. We are aware that the Yichang-Chongqing shipping route has been monopolized by foreign merchants for years, and the entire business community feels a sense of regret and despair. We are pleased to hear that your association has united to support Chinese ships, which provides an opportunity for Chinese ships to recover. We are delighted to hear this news. However, how can we resist the temptation of foreign ships' price-cutting competition? If Chinese ships are insufficient to load all goods, how can we properly allocate them? We rely on your insightful planning and are confident that you have good strategies. We hope you will provide detailed methods so that the whole country can follow suit. This is what we truly hope for. Shanghai Chamber of Commerce, Zhen, Seal.

Japanese Commercial Official Announces Foreign Trade 161

The Japanese Commercial Counselor's Office in Shanghai received a telegram from Tokyo on September 12 stating that Japan's exports in August totaled 100.7 million yen, exceeding imports by a total of 20 million yen. From January to August of this year, the import surplus reached 82 million yen, a decrease of 92 million yen compared to the same period last year. In August, Japan's total export value to China was 30 million yen, with a surplus of 14 million yen.

Developing Industry and Commerce and Labor-Capital Coordination 163

Wang Yansong's Speech Yesterday

Yesterday morning at 10:00 AM, the Third District Party Headquarters of this city invited Mr. Wang Yansong, Supervisory Committee Member of the City Party Headquarters and Standing Committee Member of the City Chamber of Commerce, to give a speech on Party principles at the wireless broadcasting station of the Da Zhonghua Electric Company on Nanjing Road. Mr. Wang's topic was "Developing Industry and Commerce and Labor-Capital Coordination." His speech was as follows: Today, I am honored to be invited by the Third District Party Headquarters of this city to come here and, in front of the self-installed wireless broadcasting station of the Da Zhonghua Electric Company, have an indirect conversation with the elders, brothers, sisters, and daughters of the entire city. What is called an indirect conversation? Because you can only hear the voice but cannot see the face, which is different from ordinary direct lectures. However, I feel that even in a great citizens' assembly, the audience has never been as large as it is today. Therefore, although I have not met you today, I am very happy and excited. The topic I want to talk about today is (Developing Industry and Commerce and Labor-Capital Coordination), because this issue is very important. It not only concerns industry and commerce themselves, but also has a close relationship with the survival of the entire nation. Therefore, I specifically raise it for everyone to discuss. Now, when it comes to this topic of (Developing Industry and Commerce and Labor-Capital Coordination), we should divide it into two parts. One part is (Developing Industry and Commerce), and the other part is (Labor-Capital Coordination). But why put these two parts together? Because one is the (cause) and the other is the (effect). In other words, (Labor-Capital Coordination) is the (cause), and (Developing Industry and Commerce) is the (effect). If we cannot first solve the problem of Labor-Capital Coordination and try to force the development of industry and commerce, then it is like climbing a tree to catch fish, which is absolutely impossible. Now, China is facing internal and external troubles, natural disasters, and man-made disasters, which are intertwined and make us feel overwhelmed. As for the domestic industry and commerce, there is really no vitality to speak of, and labor and capital still cannot understand and cooperate with each other. Everyone sees that there is no day in the newspaper without incidents of labor-capital disputes, and there is no day without strikes and shutdowns. But every unfortunate labor-capital dispute that occurs always results in both sides being hurt, and neither side can benefit. If this social disease is not treated immediately, then not only will industry and commerce have no hope of development, but even the existing industry and commerce will be swept away. Not only will the economic aggression of the great powers not be resisted, but their power will become more intense day by day. Therefore, I dare to boldly and definitively say that if China's industry and commerce continue to have labor-capital disputes, it is tantamount to self-destruction and self-seeking death. Dr. Sun Yat-sen once said that capitalists should improve the lives of workers and increase their productivity. With high productivity, workers can produce more for capitalists. On the capitalist side, they can produce more, and on the worker side, they can earn more wages. This is the harmonization of the interests of capitalists and workers, not a conflict. The reason why society evolves is because the majority of economic interests in society are harmonized, not because the majority of economic interests in society are in conflict. The harmonization of the majority of economic interests in society is to seek the interests of the majority. Only when the majority benefits can society progress. Hasn't Dr. Sun Yat-sen already indicated the great way for labor and capital to coordinate and how to coordinate? But Dr. Sun Yat-sen continued to say, (China does not have capitalists, only the distinction between large and small poverty. The labor and capital sides in China should strive under the same goal to deal with the imperialism of the great powers.) From this, we can know that the labor-capital disputes that are prevalent in society today should not have occurred. To put it bluntly, we are not even qualified to have labor-capital disputes. When I speak here, I cannot help but advise both labor and capital. Those who are in the position of labor should never simply demand increased wages, reduced working hours, and improved treatment. They should realize the reality of the decline of domestic industry and commerce, cooperate sincerely with capital, and strive together for development. They should be of one heart and one mind to resist the economic aggression of the great powers. If they force the capital side to agree to very harsh conditions, and the capital side barely agrees, if they cannot maintain their business, then there is only one way to go bankrupt. After bankruptcy, what will many workers live on? It is said that a few years ago, the workers in the silk factories and weaving factories in Hangzhou, because they demanded increased wages and reduced hours, made it impossible for the factories to maintain themselves, and dozens of factories closed down one after another. Later, many workers had nowhere to make a living and could only degrade themselves to various kinds of coolies, which was several times worse than the original wages and living conditions in the factory. Isn't this self-inflicted? Therefore, the ancients have a saying, (When the skin is gone, what will the fur be attached to?) My dear workers, you must carefully consider this saying. Furthermore, those who are in the position of capital should also be considerate of the workers. The lives of workers are mostly very difficult. The capital side should at all times try to improve the lives of the workers and never adopt oppressive measures or have the idea of exploitation. All benefits should be enjoyed openly. If we can treat the workers with such sincerity, then there is no place where labor and capital cannot cooperate. In short, capital cannot exist without labor, and labor cannot exist without capital. The two are interdependent. If the labor and capital sides in our country can accept my advice now and work together to develop their own industry and commerce, then not only will the existing industry and commerce be thriving, but new industries will surely erupt like spring bamboo shoots. At that time, the future of China's industry and commerce will be bright, and how difficult will it be to resist the economic aggression of the great powers from thousands of miles away? That's all.

Fisheries Bureau Receives a Large Batch of Military Equipment 165

Since the establishment of the Fisheries Bureau of the Ministry of Industry's Jiangsu-Zhejiang District in May of this year, Director Han Yougang has been keen on rectifying matters related to ocean protection, frequently personally leading his affiliated ships on patrols. Therefore, the bandit atmosphere along the coast has recently been slightly suppressed compared to before. However, the original firearms of the bureau's ships are insufficient for use, and repeated telegrams have been sent to the Ministry of Industry requesting replenishment. It is reported that yesterday, water machine guns, rifles, wooden-cased guns, and bullets were received in large numbers and will be distributed to the patrol ships for use immediately. It is also reported that steel cannons and handguns will also be received one after another soon. From now on, the fishermen of Jiangsu and Zhejiang provinces, who have long suffered from banditry, will be protected.

Contracts Required for Using Road Land 166

Proclamation by the Two Roads Bureau Directors

Guo Chengen, Director of the Two Roads Bureau, issued a proclamation yesterday stating: For the matter of proclamation, it has been found that there are already regulations for renting land along this road. Any use of road land without a signed lease is considered a violation and encroachment, which cannot be tolerated. Furthermore, failure to pay rent on time after signing a lease, resulting in long-term accumulation, is also a violation of the regulations, causing inconvenience. Therefore, this notice is issued. From now on, whether they are workers on this road or local farmers, if they rent land along this road, they must strictly abide by the regulations, sign a lease, and pay rent on time. Those who refuse to comply and delay payment will have their rented land taken back by this bureau for the sake of maintaining property rights and public funds and will be rented out again. At the same time, they will be sent to the county for legal action to serve as a warning to others. Do not say that you were not warned. This proclamation is crucial.

Huang Yunkui was elected as the director of academic affairs for the west district school, and Huang Bingkui was elected as the director of academic affairs for the east district school. The teaching staff was also selected, and the directors will contact them for publication.

The Bund's High Tide Keeps Warehouses Busy 168

Taking precautions

Moving goods one after another

The tide in the Huangpu River has been high in recent days. Yesterday morning, the tide rose so high that the water on the Bund reached the shore. In the afternoon, it rained lightly, and the warehouses along the Huangpu River, fearing a repeat of last month's major flood, hired workers to move their goods to other places or to the upper floors for storage as a precaution, and they were very busy.

Improved Clothing Exhibition Opens 169

Held at Yipinsan yesterday

Over a thousand guests attended

Six groups, including the Shanghai Family Innovation Society, the China Vocational Education Society, the Sanyou Industrial Company, the Women's Department of the Puyi Society, the China Women's Temperance Union, and the Joint Association of Women's Vocational Schools, held an improved clothing exhibition yesterday at the Yipinsan on Xizang Road. Over two thousand guests from all walks of life attended. After ringing the bell to open the meeting and performing the rituals, the chairpersons of the presidium, Yang Weiyu, Shen Jiucheng, and Liu Wang Liming, successively reported on the purpose of the meeting, elaborating on the inappropriateness of traditional Chinese clothing and the reasons for reform. They also reported on the new clothing fabrics recently launched by Sanyou Company, which are all domestic goods, hoping for criticism and guidance from all walks of life. After the reports, there was a parade of new-style clothing, with a total of seven types: little brothers, little sisters, middle school boys' wear, female students' wear, adult wear, elderly men's and women's wear, and Sanyou Company employees' world wear. They paraded around the circle in order. After the parade, Xu Peihuang, Pan Gongzhan, Hu Yinghua, Tao Baichuan, Zhao Zhengping, Lin Kanghou, and Wang Xiaolai successively gave speeches, praising each item exhibited today and hoping to increase the production of domestic clothing fabrics so that improved clothing and the promotion of domestic goods can develop in parallel. Wang Xiaolai's twelfth son, Wang Daren (nine years old), spoke on his behalf. He was eloquent and composed, which was greatly praised by the audience. Next, Deng Shouyu, a female student from Xingzhong Elementary School, gave a speech urging all walks of life to improve clothing and promote domestic goods. After the speech, Li Xianmin played the piano, Yu Yixuan sang, and Ms. Niu Xinxia danced the Charleston. The Aiqun Women's School of Lin Yin Elementary School successively performed various excellent dances. Wang Qingxun played the harmonica, etc., to add to the fun. Finally, a photo was taken and the meeting adjourned. After the opening ceremony, a luncheon was held, and after the meal, the exhibition was open to the public. Visitors from all walks of life continued to arrive in an endless stream. It is reported that all the items on display are made of domestic raw materials, are brave and martial in style, economical, sturdy, light, comfortable, and beautiful in color. On the spot, guests purchased many sets of various new-style clothes. Sanyou Company decided to donate the proceeds from the sale to disaster relief.

Qian Shenzhi proposed that, according to reports, there was talk of opening the Dongba Dam in Gaochun County, which concerns the lives and property of the people of the Suzhou and Songjiang regions. An urgent motion should be made. It was decided to send a telegram to the provincial government, appealing for a halt to prevent repercussions. The telegram read as follows: "To Chairman of the Provincial Government, Director of Civil Affairs, and Director of Construction: Upon investigation, the Gaochun Shangba, known as Dongba, protects Suzhou, Songjiang, Changzhou, and Zhenjiang. The dam's foundation has long been in disrepair. Recently, due to standing water in Gao Shao and other places, some have advocated opening Dongba, harming neighbors. The regions are greatly alarmed. This dam was opened on May 26th, Daoguang 29th year of the Qing Dynasty. At that time, fields in Suzhou, Songjiang, Changzhou, and Zhenjiang were flooded, and many died. Elders still speak of it with lingering fear. We urgently appeal to you to immediately order Gaochun County and the local water conservancy authorities to do everything possible to prevent it. Our people are your fish, and you should not bear to see disaster realized. Respectfully, Zhou Shixiong, Zhang Yipeng, Lu Zhaokun, Chairman of the Shanghai Suzhou Native Place Association, and all members."

Representatives of the Seawall Committee Petition the Provincial Government 178

Tang Weizhi, Zhu Kaichou, Hong Jingping

The seawall works in the northern regions of Wusong, Taicang, and Baoshan counties have suffered damage from the hurricane and storm surge since the evening of the 25th of last month. According to investigations, approximately 1,600 zhang have been affected, with the section near the Daotang Temple in Taicang County being the most severely damaged. Local officials and gentry have jointly appealed for aid and are currently engaged in urgent repairs. The Taicang County Government specifically raised the issue for discussion at the county administration meeting the day before yesterday (the 11th). As a result, it was decided to organize a seawall committee, which was established on the spot, and its charter was approved. Tang Weizhi, Zhu Kaichou, Hong Jingping, Zhu Qingzhao, Hu Cuishi, Lu Songlun, Jiang Yuren, Qian Chunyi, and Wu Xingsan were appointed as members. Tang, Zhu, and Hong were elected as standing committee members to handle all seawall-related matters. Given the urgency of the seawall situation, the Party Headquarters, the Chamber of Commerce, and the Property Office jointly telegraphed the Department of Construction and the Bureau of Water Conservancy, sternly instructing Xue Zhaoshu, director of the Jiangnan Seawall Works Office, to take full responsibility for the emergency repair work and to expedite the process. Tang Weizhi, Zhu Kaichou, and Hong Jingping were publicly nominated as representatives to petition the provincial government. They set off yesterday.

Foreman Kidnapped 179

Walking Down from Teahouse, Kidnapped by Bandits

Bandits Take Shen's Bookkeeper

Six People Driven Off Mid-Route, Bandits Escape

Threatening Letters Received Three Years Ago

Shen Shengda, a native of Pudong, is a pile-driving foreman for Shen Shengji, specializing in this industry for many years. Many major buildings in Shanghai have had their foundations driven by him. He lives at No. 140, New Kangli, Yangshupu Road, and owns a car for transportation, with license plate numbers 4741 in the concession and 1886 in the municipal government. Yesterday, around 6:00 PM, he and his son Shen Wenxin and four bookkeepers went to the Yiletian Teahouse on Hubei Road, driven by chauffeur Wu Linsheng. Upon arrival, Wu parked the car in front of the Xiqing Pool on Jiujiang Road, facing east. Shen and the others went upstairs to Yiletian for tea. Around 7:15 PM, Shen Shengda and the six others finished and went back downstairs, returning to the car. Just as the engine started, four bandits suddenly blocked the car. One, dressed in gray, occupied the driver's seat. Another, dressed in blue, held a box cannon, forbidding anyone in the car from making a sound, saying they were just borrowing the car to rob earth and had no other intention. The other two, dressed in black long gowns and armed with weapons, sat on top of Shen and the others, pinning them down. Then, the bandit driving stepped on the gas and drove straight ahead, south on Fujian Road, west on Avenue Edward VII, south on Danshui Road, to Avenue Cardinal Mercier in the French Concession, where the car stopped. The bandits first pushed one of the four bookkeepers, surnamed Zhang, off the car, then kept watch over the hostage Shen Shengda, drove off the remaining people, and sped away towards Avenue Dubail, quickly disappearing from sight. Shen's son Wenxin and the others rushed to report to the French Concession police and notified the Shanghai Municipal Police, ordering all police stations to be on alert. However, as of late at night, there were still no leads. Shen Shengda is forty-eight years old and has three sons, Wenxin being the eldest. The car is a Buick, purchased some years ago. The chauffeur was originally Pan Gengsheng, but he recently took sick leave and was temporarily replaced by Wu Linsheng for only about ten days. Three years ago, Shen had contracted to drive piles for the Customs House on the Bund of Hankou Road. At that time, someone coveted his wealth and sent a threatening letter demanding 50,000 yuan. After reporting to the police, four suspects were apprehended and convicted by the court.

Hou Guangdi and Wife's Second Divorce Lawsuit 180

Hou Himself Files for Divorce

His Wife Requests Cohabitation and Support

Hou Guangdi, a Western doctor, was involved in a divorce lawsuit with his wife Hou Wu Hailun last year. The matter was resolved through reconciliation, and they remained on good terms. Now, just a year later, Hou has filed for a second divorce. Wu, upon learning of this, has also retained lawyer Hong Shihao to sue Hou in the First Special District Court for coercing her into signing documents and for abandonment and failure to provide support, requesting a ruling for cohabitation and support, and revocation of the illegal documents, among other things. The original pleadings, once filled with tender emotions, are now recorded as follows:

"I, the petitioner, worked as a teacher in Qingpu, Shanghai, Nanjing, and other places. On February 10th of the Republican year ten, I was engaged to Mr. Cai. However, before the marriage could take place, Mr. Cai passed away prematurely. At that time, the defendant was friendly with Mr. Cai, and seeing that I was young, he took the opportunity to use his seductive tricks, making countless vows and pledges. I initially paid no attention, but seeing his sincere attitude and extremely enthusiastic performance, I could not remain unmoved, especially as I was newly widowed and felt lost in the vast world. Moreover, I was convinced that he had ended his relationship with Miss Weng, his previous lover, and I was thus bewitched and associated with him, eventually becoming husband and wife. In the eleventh year, in September, I became pregnant and gave birth to our eldest daughter, Xi Rui. Over the past ten years, I have given birth to one son and two daughters. I married the defendant hoping to grow old together, and I always submitted and complied with his wishes. However, the defendant's love for me changed with the waxing and waning of my beauty. Having managed the household for years and undergone several childbirths, my beauty was naturally no longer comparable to when I first married. The defendant, growing tired of me, resumed his old habits of seeking pleasure, using the same tricks he had used to seduce me on others. Within months, he openly kept a mistress in a golden house at No. 277 Yanqingli, Xiamen Road. When I intervened slightly, he became enraged and his mask was torn off. He fabricated stories and filed for divorce in your honorable court. At that time, I had just given birth and was devastated by the sudden blow. The defendant, with a heart of a serpent, took advantage of my vulnerable state to coerce me into signing documents, threatening to harm me if I did not comply. Under such oppressive force, I had no choice but to obey his wishes, hoping that he would change his mind, considering our nine years of marriage. To this day, I am still unaware of the contents of the documents. Afterwards, we resumed our lives without incident, and he, knowing that his divorce lawsuit was untenable, withdrew it (Year 19, Personal Character No. 52). This spring, the defendant's lust knew no bounds, and he had an affair with our female servant. Considering the matter too outrageous and easily laughed at, I dismissed her. The defendant, unwilling to part with his new favorite, harbored malicious intentions and again forced me to sign a document, forcing me to live separately. As a woman, I was powerless to resist and had no choice but to leave in distress with my three children. It has been many days since then, and not only has he failed to provide support, he has treated me as a stranger. Just as I was about to file a lawsuit, the defendant preemptively filed a lawsuit, claiming I owed him money, hoping to easily erase our marital relationship. His actions are truly outrageous. When the defendant was destitute, I, compelled by marital duty, generously provided assistance. Now that I am older and my beauty has faded, he has become so heartless and extreme. This is intolerable in both emotion and law. Therefore, I recount the events and implore for relief, requesting that the defendant's lawsuit be rejected, that he be ordered to fulfill his obligation of cohabitation and support, and that the illegally written documents be revoked. If evidence of bigamy is discovered, I request that it be reported together to uphold ethics and maintain social order. Respectfully submitted."

Tragic Death of a Long-Term Servant to be Sent to Court 183

Twenty-Eight Stores Guarantee Two Painters

The case of Ling Xiangxiang, a sedan carrier for famous doctor Xia Yingtang, who was hacked to death and his body burned to cover up the crime, was solved by the First Branch of the Second District. The suspect, Gao Asan, confessed to the involvement of painters Zhang Yongquan and Ye Xufu, who were arrested and presented to the Public Security Bureau. The Judicial Science Department interrogated them, and Gao Asan maintained his previous confession. However, Zhang Yongquan and Ye Xufu claimed that they were asleep on the night of the incident and did not go out. Zhang Yongquan claimed to be staying at the Ruixing Store, and Ye Xufu claimed to be staying at the Yuanshunxing Store, and that they did not leave after 10:00 PM that night, which could be verified. At the same time, twenty-eight stores, including Jinruixing, Yishunxing, Dexingxiang, Hanyongxing, Zheng Xiangji, La Dachang, and Huyuanxing on Fangbang Road, submitted a joint guarantee, proving that they did not go out and still went to the Xia family to work the next day, and there was no false information, and they could not enter the Xia family's gate at night. After reviewing the documents, the Judicial Science Department decided to submit the case to the court for verification and investigation by the District Court, pending a ruling.

Cao Ayuan Missing for Seven Days, Body Found in Vegetable Field 184

Cao Ayuan, a resident of Caojiazhai near the Baoshan Fort north of Wusong, over fifty years old, who worked as a vegetable farmer, suddenly left home one week and did not return by nightfall. His family searched everywhere without success. Initially, they suspected that he had gone to visit relatives in Liuhang, so they did not pay much attention and waited for his return. The day before yesterday morning, a resident of the same village, Mr. Cao, was searching in a nearby vegetable field and found a corpse. The head was buried in the mud. Examining the clothes, he recognized it as Cao Ayuan, who had been missing for seven days. He immediately ran to inform his family, who came to identify the body without error. The body was then collected, but it was already badly decomposed. It is said that the deceased had no previous illness, and this time it may have been a sudden death due to an acute illness.

The woman Xue Shen Shi, hired a lawyer to file a criminal lawsuit in the Second Special District Court, stating that her husband, Xue Huicheng, had jointly opened a medicinal materials business with Yan Ruishun when he was alive. Her husband had several thousand taels of cash that he had lent to Yan Ruishun, and several thousand pounds of medicinal bark stored in the business. Unfortunately, after her husband died of illness last year, all the goods and loans were embezzled by the defendant alone. All attempts to reason with him had failed. She relies entirely on this money to live, so how can she allow him to appropriate it? Therefore, she is unwilling to accept this and has filed a lawsuit requesting an investigation. Yan Ruishun claimed that all the goods in the business were recorded in the account books and that he would not dare to embezzle them. He requested a clear investigation. The judge instructed both parties to retain their positions and await further review at a later date.

Jiang Water is Ruthless, Only Son Dies Tragically 186

Xu Qiaokun is the Heir to Three Branches

Old Mother Cries to the Huangpu River

Xu Qiaokun, a dockworker, 26 years old, lived at No. 28 Lantou, Pudong Landu Town. Yesterday morning at 6:00 AM, he was carrying goods from a ship to the shore at the Taikoo Company's No. 4 foreign warehouse dock when he accidentally lost his footing on the gangplank and fell into the Huangpu River and drowned. His body sank and disappeared without a trace. Upon learning of this, his mother, Xing Shi, rushed to the dock and cried loudly to the Huangpu River, almost fainting, as Qiaokun was the only son of three family branches. Those who saw her were saddened.

Fan Lantian Sued by Wife for Bigamy and Abandonment 187

Trial to be Held this Afternoon

Fan Qu Shi, a woman residing at No. 35 Zhen'anli, Guangzhao Road, Zhabei, and her younger sister-in-law Fan Xiaozhong, recently retained lawyer Shen Yong to file a lawsuit in the First District Court against Fan Lantian, residing at the Liangchen Haoyou Society on Beijing Road, for the crimes of bigamy and abandonment. The lawsuit stated that Fan Qu Shi is the defendant's legal wife, married to him in the eighth year of the Republic through matchmakers Lin Laiquan and Li Fukui. Although they were not very harmonious at first, they were still compatible. In the thirteenth year of the Republic, the defendant had an affair with a woman surnamed Zhang, and secretly married her in a hotel in Shanghai in April of the fourteenth year of the Republic. They have now had two sons and a daughter. Starting in October of that year, claiming that she could not bear children, he took the Zhang woman as a concubine and brought her to their old house in Pudong, forcing her to live with her and forcing her to give up the main room to live in a side room with her younger sister Xiaozhong. If she refused, he threatened to cut off her food and clothing and ordered her uncle Fan Xinfu to divorce her. Because she refused, the abuse increased. Initially, he gave her seven yuan per month for food and clothing, but later he made her share the seven yuan with her younger sister Xiaozhong, while he and his new wife lived in luxury, feasting and wearing fine clothes. She spent her days hungry and her years without fresh clothes, treated like a slave. In September of the sixteenth year of the Republic, her younger sister Xiaozhong, also unable to bear the lack of food and clothing, left to work as a laborer. Considering that in the winter of the fourteenth year of the Republic, her younger sister Xiaozhong was already twenty years old and there had been marriage proposals, the defendant declared that if Xiaozhong married, the monthly seven yuan would be stopped. Although she had asked people to intercede, the defendant said that the monthly seven yuan was for his sister, not for her. Xiaozhong thought that if she married, her sister-in-law would have no food or clothing, so it was better to live because of her than to die for her, so she refused to marry and shared the hardships with her sister-in-law. Therefore, in September of the sixteenth year of the Republic, she bid farewell to everyone in the house and went to Shanghai with her sister-in-law to work and support themselves. The defendant was happy with their departure and wanted to stop paying the monthly seven yuan. After the relatives protested against his actions, he gave them two rooms that collected eight yuan in rent each month in Shanghai Zhabei. However, the rent collection fee required one or two yuan per month, making it difficult to collect the rent and barely enough to support their food and clothing, which forced them to find a way to support themselves. After arriving in Shanghai, the defendant treated them as if they were strangers, not treating his younger sister as a sister and not fulfilling his obligation to find her a husband, and not treating his wife as a wife and showing no kindness. Forced into this situation, they could only rely on the monthly rent of eight yuan as a basis and supplement it with their labor income. However, they came from a well-off family and were not used to working and living, and their situation was extremely difficult. She had begged her husband's brothers for assistance, but they did not even give her a glance. Now, the Zhabei tenant has stopped paying the rent, making it difficult for them to support themselves and wanting to leave them to die. The court, based on the lawsuit, has scheduled a trial for this afternoon (the 14th) in the second criminal court by Judge Feng.
