Reader Correspondence

News from Miss Zhang Fengwen 193

I have an unexpected matter to report to you, and I ask you to resolve it for me. I am a woman who grew up in Shanghai and received a secondary education. However, my fiancé is an uneducated country bumpkin who cannot support himself. Six years ago, my father's business failed. My fiancé's father not only voluntarily waived all of his creditor's rights but also provided a large sum of money for my father to start his business again, stating that it was in consideration of the engagement agreement. My father, of course, could not object. At that time, I was only fifteen years old and did not fully understand the world. Although I was somewhat dissatisfied, I did not express it formally. Now I am older, and the old saying "when a boy grows up, he should marry; when a girl grows up, she should be married" is about to become a reality through a series of rituals. I, the unfortunate sacrifice, am absolutely against it. My mother often tempts me with tales of his family's thousands of acres of land and numerous houses, saying that even if he does not work, we will not starve. My father, looking pitiful, says with tears in his eyes, "If I don't repay the debt, my conscience will be troubled. If I don't do this, I will have to experience the flavor of an iron window." My brother, on the other hand, is absolutely against it. He says that debts should be repaid with money, and I should not be used as collateral. Alas, kind sir, my wedding date is in December this winter. The short time of three months feels like a flash of lightning. From then on, I will not only have no happy days, but my life's happiness will be eliminated invisibly. Great editor, you will solve this problem because you are the messenger of happiness for people. There may be more than one woman in the world like me. Please save me and help me! I hope to receive a response in the newspaper.

(Reply) Let me first tell you the law. Article 975 of the Civil Code states that "an engagement cannot be forcibly enforced." If you do not want to, no one can force you. Moreover, Article 972 of the Civil Code states that "an engagement should be entered into voluntarily by the parties concerned." If you have not yet formally expressed your intention, this problem may still be resolved. However, you must find a way to make your father understand your difficulties. Most importantly, you must not be pessimistic. Your thoughts are of the highest and purest kind. You should use the utmost sincerity, courage, and determination to explain the advantages, disadvantages, blessings, and misfortunes of the future to your father with a thousand points of earnestness and a thousand points of clarity and firmness, repeatedly. There are no parents in the world who do not love their children. According to the law, the final decision rests with you. There is no need to be pessimistic.

News from Mr. Zeng Gui 194

Being dominated by the family's economic situation has deprived me of the opportunity to further my education. Recalling the past, when I was in elementary school, I didn't pay attention to any of my subjects and found them boring. However, after entering middle school, two things prompted me to study hard. The first was the extreme shortage of family finances, and the second was the deep understanding that my studies were temporary and for technical needs. After fighting for a year, my interest in studying was aroused, and I became very interested in all kinds of books. Now it's time for me to graduate. Here, I want to ask, should I get a job or further my education? However, if I get a job, not only will my distant ambitions become a bubble, but it will also be difficult to find a job. Conversely, the tuition for further education is nowhere to be found, making it even harder for the family to support itself. In this situation, please help me resolve it.

(Reply) The statement that "distant ambitions become a bubble after getting a job" is wrong. The noblest thing in life is "earning one's own living." That is why it is called "the sacredness of occupation." Even if you graduate from university, you still have to get a job. Moreover, getting a job does not necessarily hinder further education. Not to mention that you can attend supplementary schools in your spare time while working, but even if you work for a year or two and then go back to school, you will benefit from both economically and practically. As the saying goes, "Those who excel in officialdom then learn," which is the same principle.

Since the tuition for further education cannot be found, employment is naturally the first priority. Finding a job is certainly not easy, but even university graduates have to go through this difficulty. Why not ask relatives and friends for help now and try to find a way?

Actually, you have already gone down the wrong path. If you cannot afford to go to university, you should have entered a vocational school when you entered high school. If you cannot afford to go to high school, you should have entered a vocational school when you entered junior high school. Unfortunately, there are too many people in society who go down the wrong path. After graduating from an ordinary junior high school or an ordinary high school, it is naturally very difficult to find a job because you have no skills.

News from Mr. Xia Changyu 195

Changyu was an out-of-school youth. He is now twenty-three years old. During this year's summer vacation, he asked a friend to introduce him to Mr. Wang Xishen, the principal of the Zhengfeng College of Literature, and he was granted permission to enroll in the school. However, his family forbade him from doing so. Since this disappointment, Changyu has been discouraged in everything. Now, after his family's consideration, they have advised him to study medicine (traditional Chinese medicine) or commerce. However, neither is close to his interests, and hope of studying has faded. Medicine and commerce are bound to neglect one or the other, making it a dilemma. Changyu is temporarily unclear about which path to take and has sent this letter specifically, hoping for a quick reply.

(Reply) Young people should choose a career or a major based on the following four criteria: (1) what is closest to their nature, (2) what they have a special talent for, (3) what the family has a particularly suitable environment for, and (4) what society needs. Young people should carefully examine and choose, obtain the consent of their parents, and then decide. Generally speaking, after the age of fifteen or sixteen, you should feel this yourself. You are already twenty-three years old and should have the ability to choose for yourself. Studying medicine and studying commerce are very different. Which one to choose, you should examine yourself according to the above four criteria and explain it to your family very sincerely. If you speak reasonably, kind parents will not refuse to follow. However, whether entering the College of Literature can be relied upon as a career in the future is also a question you should consider. Our position can only put forward some principles to remind you and cannot solve it for you specifically. You must forgive us.

Rules for Reader Correspondence in Shen Bao 196

The staff of this newspaper firmly believe that readers have many personal questions that need to be discussed and resolved urgently. Based on the spirit of serving society, the staff is willing to act as advisors and offer sincere suggestions in writing. If readers can obtain appropriate solutions, reduce difficulties, and increase happiness, how can we not be delighted?

1. The questions that readers want to discuss with the staff of this newspaper are temporarily limited to three categories: education, career, and marriage.

2. When corresponding, please first state your surname, given name, gender, age, occupation (or the school year and grade), place of origin, and mailing address (it is advisable to provide detailed information for continued correspondence in case the previous letter does not arrive). Then, start a new paragraph and state the question you want to discuss. The writing should be detailed, accurate, and easy to understand the true meaning. On the outside of the envelope, please write "Shen Bao Reader Correspondence Department" and attach a sufficient number of return postage stamps as a voucher.

3. The following is how this newspaper handles received letters:

A. Respect the wishes of readers. Any letter that states a wish not to be answered in the newspaper or to disclose their name will be complied with.

B. If the letter does not state how to reply, but the staff believes that answering one person has value for everyone's reference, it will be disclosed in the newspaper.

C. If the letter states a wish to be answered in the newspaper, but it is limited by space, we can only choose to disclose the main points or not disclose it at all, or because the question is still under consideration, we have to delay the disclosure. Please forgive us. However, if we cannot answer in the newspaper, we will still answer by mail.

Free Talk

Gatherings in the Unswept Courtyard

Mr. Banana Leaf Fan 198

Mr. Banana Leaf Fan is named after fanning a banana leaf fan. Many people fan banana leaf fans. Who among the farmers cooling off shirtless in front of thatched huts doesn't fan a banana leaf fan? Why is it that only Mr. Banana Leaf Fan has a name and no one else? This is not accidental. Everyone else fans round fans and folding fans, but Mr. Banana Leaf Fan exclusively fans a banana leaf fan. People see Mr. Banana Leaf Fan and immediately see a banana leaf fan, and seeing a banana leaf fan immediately brings Mr. Banana Leaf Fan to mind. Involuntarily, they associate Mr. Banana Leaf Fan with the banana leaf fan. Over time, even Mr. Banana Leaf Fan's name is forgotten, but the banana leaf fan is not forgotten. Thinking of Mr. Banana Leaf Fan brings the banana leaf fan to mind, and thinking of the banana leaf fan brings Mr. Banana Leaf Fan to mind. Inevitably, naturally, everyone calls Mr. Banana Leaf Fan by this name. The reason why Mr. Banana Leaf Fan fans a banana leaf fan among a crowd of round fans is not to deliberately be different, but because the banana leaf fan has great uses and he doesn't want to see it buried. Someone may ask Mr. Banana Leaf Fan about the banana leaf fan, and Mr. Banana Leaf Fan will reply: "When I run on the road under the scorching sun, I don't need to wear a hat; when I encounter rain along the way, I don't need to open an umbrella; when I am tired, I can sit down anywhere and have a ready-made cushion; when it gets cool in the middle of the night, it is lighter and more convenient than a blanket when covering my stomach; when it is unbearably hot, one person can fan the fan and everyone can share the cool breeze: all of this depends on this banana leaf fan." Mr. Banana Leaf Fan has a friend who teaches children in the countryside. He usually doesn't like to meddle in other people's business, but when a country bumpkin is bullied, he asks his friend for advice, and his friend will do his best to come up with a plan for them. His friend often walks in the mountains and forests while waving a banana leaf fan. Therefore, the villagers often call him Banana Leaf Kongming to distinguish him from Kongming, who fans a goose feather fan. Banana Leaf Kongming was eventually imprisoned for repeatedly fighting for justice and offending the powerful. The prison guard asked for money. Having nothing left, he reluctantly gave the prison guard his banana leaf fan. This banana leaf fan was particularly large. Mr. Banana Leaf Fan passed by the prison guard's house and saw the prison guard fanning himself with the fan. Recognizing the fan as his friend's, he bought it from the prison guard at several times the price. The banana leaf fan that Mr. Banana Leaf Fan is now carrying around in the bustling city is this one.

Anecdotes of Famous Novelist Xu Fumin 199

— Zheng Yimei

I, a person from Foshan, and Nan Tingtingchang are both seniors in the world of storytelling. At the same time, there was also Mr. Xu Fumin of Qiantang, who enjoyed considerable fame for his book "Records of Officialdom." My lodging place here has a family friendship with Mr. Xu. Yesterday, while examining old bookshelves, I found a landscape fan painted by Mr. Xu, so I am recounting his anecdotes, which are also rare stories in the world of storytelling. Mr. Xu was tall and handsome, and he frequented brothels and gambling dens, occasionally indulging in his leisure pursuits. He had a boisterous spirit and excelled at eloquence, which flowed like a river bursting its banks. He traveled as a staff member to Jiangxi and later obtained an official position in Hubei Province's salt administration through grain donation. Because of his dissolute lifestyle, he inevitably tarnished his official reputation. At that time, the Manchu official Rui Zheng held a high position and wielded great power. Mr. Xu offended him. Rui Zheng sent out his secret police to arrest him and fabricate crimes against him. Mr. Xu learned of this early and hid in a certain prefect's office. The prefect was an old friend of Mr. Xu. Rui Zheng sent soldiers to search for him, and he was only able to avoid arrest by hiding in a secret room. Before long, he secretly fled to Shanghai and wrote "Records of Officialdom" to expose Rui Zheng's secrets. The book was thorough and welcomed by readers. When the Yellow Turban Army raised the flag of rebellion in Huangpi, Hubei Province was restored. Rui Zheng fled. Mr. Xu, together with the actor Pan Yueqiao and others, arranged a new play called "Yellow Crane Tower," which also depicted Rui Zheng's scandalous history. "Yellow Crane Tower" sold out every show. They then arranged another play called "Black List Wrongs," so that those who were sunk in the black list would be startled when they saw it. It had the same purpose as Wu Jianren's "Sea of Regret." Mr. Xu also organized the "Monthly Novel" magazine with Shen Jixuan, which was published monthly and was the oldest novel magazine. Famous writers such as I, a person from Foshan, Zhou Guisheng, Tianxiaosheng, Tianxu Wosheng, Sick Man of East Asia, and Tian Lusheng all contributed articles. It was discontinued after several dozen issues. Mr. Xu's name was Zhi, and his pseudonym was Fumin. He was skilled in calligraphy and painting landscapes. He was truly a man of many talents. He died of illness in a certain year of the Republic of China, and those who heard of it regretted it.

After the meal, they visited the business place for a week. Those who purchased goods were very enthusiastic. I returned and wrote this record.

A Small Study of Ms. Chen Qianyi 201

Many of the popular terms in recent times have originated from transliterations of English words. The origin of these transliterations mostly comes from Shanghai. Shanghai is the first to open up to new trends and has a wider range of knowledge. When a certain thing appears, there is no way to name it at first, so it is called by a convenient transliteration. Over time, it becomes a common term. For example, the telephone is also called "delüfeng," which is a transliteration of the English word "telephone." However, sometimes the Shanghai dialect is different from the dialects of the interior and distant provinces, and those who do not know the original English word often mispronounce it. For example, "shuiting," which is used for winter heating, is a transliteration of "steam." Its meaning is water vapor. In Shanghai, "shui" (water) is pronounced "si," which is close to the original sound. However, when it is pronounced in the Jiangbei dialect or the Mandarin dialect, "shui" is not pronounced "si," which does not match the original word. Moreover, "shuiting" is often confused with "shuimending," and it is suspected to be an abbreviation of "shuimending." This is even more of a mistake. Little do they know that "shuimending" is cement, which is a transliteration of "cement." It is only because the transliteration was not very accurate at the beginning that it shares two characters with "shuiting" today. In fact, it should be transliterated as "ximente," which is not very different from the original. Another example is the "shafa" chair. In the Shanghai dialect, "sha" is pronounced "shu," which is consistent with the pronunciation of the original word "sofa." However, it is pronounced differently by people in Jiangbei and distant provinces. The Western medicine morphine is pronounced "ma" as "mao" in the Shanghai dialect, so it matches. Another example is "paishi" (pass), where "pai" is pronounced "pa" in the Shanghai dialect, which is also the same as the original meaning. If you pronounce them in a different place, they are all not the original sounds. This is something to be aware of. In the future, the invention of nouns in Shanghai should preferably use Mandarin transliterations, and should not be entirely in the Suzhou-Shanghai dialect, so as to avoid different pronunciations and different tones in other places. For example, the word tones in a play must be sung in the dialects of Pingchu and other places. If it is sung in the Shanghai dialect, it will inevitably have the drawback of singing "xiaodongren chuangxiale" (the little Dongren broke into it) as "xiaodongning chuang'ele" (the little Dongning broke from hunger). What do the gentlemen and ladies of Shanghai think of this?

Other popular terms, such as "luoji," are a transliteration of "logic." Its meaning is the theory of reasoning in grammar. Recently, some people with shallow views mistakenly believe that logic is a person's name. How great is their mistake? Even some elementary school teachers in the interior do not know the truth and cannot explain it, leading to the spread of misinformation and misleading children. Special attention should be paid to this and it should be refuted. Another example is "dike tuituo," which is a transliteration of "dictator." It seems to mean a leader with the ability to command. Also, the two characters "beige" are a transliteration of "boycott." Modern writing often has words such as "beige wenti" (boycott issue), which means the issue of boycotting foreign goods. However, the transliteration of "boycott" as "beige" is rather far-fetched. It seems to be translated by people from the northern provinces. However, if we know that its source is a transliteration, we can avoid excessive criticism. However, if people in Zhenjiang read it, the character "ge" is read as the local sound of "jia," which is directly contrary to the original word, making it incomprehensible for a while. Those who study local dialects must pay attention to this. (Move funds from entertainment to disaster relief)

The American Film Industry (I) 202

— Ji Ping

Drama expert Hong Shen traveled to the United States this spring. His mission was to purchase new equipment, hire actors, and investigate the American film industry for the Star Film Company. He lived in Hollywood for some time, carefully studying it and gaining much insight. Speaking of the three words "Hollywood," everyone knows that it is the birthplace of American film art and a special area for the film industry. Many famous stars and directors are concentrated in one place. Their lives are very extravagant, romantic, and mysterious. Therefore, the place of Hollywood also changes customs and habits, which is very different from other places. Recently, many film practitioners have applied to the leaders of the film industry to reorganize Hollywood, reduce the shocking salaries of stars and directors, and save the wasteful expenses that are laughable. They believe that this can promote a more populist Hollywood. But whether this can be achieved in reality is still questionable. Mr. Hong Shen has now returned to China. I asked him about the current situation of the Hollywood film industry. He said that in recent years, due to overproduction and economic decline in the United States, many people have lost their jobs. The film industry has also been greatly affected and has declined sharply. Now, I will introduce his words to readers.

American filmmakers have recently paid much attention to "sound emotionalization." This means that in sound films, in addition to singing and music, the dialogue and speech must not only be clear but also have the sound of speech be circuitous and tactful, circuitous, and tactful, and can express emotions. This is not an easy thing to achieve. The first thing is to train the actors' pronunciation and intonation to be correct. Therefore, major film companies have hired pronunciation teachers to be responsible for guidance. The old silent film stars (silent films are silent films) have now declined. Some people compare Ms. Hu Die to Mary Pickford. Those who heard this were greatly surprised. Mary Pickford, although she was popular for a long time, has now joined the ranks of those who are immersed in decline. Lionel Barrymore has achieved great success with his old stage experience. His new film, "A Free Soul," is his proud work. Because film actors spend a longer time preparing to practice pronunciation, they continue to act on set during the set-up time. This is a remedy for the company's time economy.

The equipment in China's major theaters simply cannot compare with the top-class theaters in the United States. Often, old movie machines that are considered obsolete abroad are slightly modified and transported to China and installed in the best theaters. Therefore, when it comes to pronunciation, Chinese theaters are far behind foreign theaters. Other things need not be said.

Rotary Club Storytelling Association

The Wife of the Official (13) 203

— Jiang Hongjiao

Madam Li also knew clearly that constantly receiving Mr. Chen's money and things was not proper. Although Mr. Chen willingly gave them, and she did not ask for them. She felt that if her husband found out, there would definitely be an explosive scene, and others would not understand, and she would become someone rejected by all of society in the future. But her situation was really difficult, and she really couldn't refuse Mr. Chen's kindness. If she refused, it would definitely make Mr. Chen unhappy. She didn't know why she was becoming more and more indifferent to her husband, but so close to one of her husband's friends, hoping he would be happy. She didn't dare to formally propose a divorce to her husband, because even after divorcing, she might not be able to formally marry Mr. Chen. Mr. Chen has a wife, and his wife is very fierce. If I don't divorce and secretly have an affair with Mr. Chen, that would not only be unfair to my husband, but also to my own status and reputation. According to the current situation, she knew very well, and they both understood, that they had truly reached the stage of love. They were able to restrain themselves, and never made any displays of love, but in each other's hearts, they had already planted the seeds of love very high and large. They had both pondered, is this great and faithful? Or is it a sin? They were still hesitant, wavering, building up momentum, not daring to rush to the front lines; what bound them was still a kind of old morality commonly used in society.

Mr. Li and Madam Chen were ultimately romantics. Their views were the opposite of Mr. Chen's and Madam Li's. They felt that if the relationship between husband and wife was only limited to nominal constraints without true love, it was immoral; it was okay to find a suitable object outside the constraints of name. So when Mr. Li kissed her hand, she didn't refuse. In the darkness of the movie theater, when he kissed her forehead, she accepted it happily. When they hugged tightly while dancing, she smiled sweetly at him. Beyond that, whatever expressions of love there were, she certainly wouldn't make Mr. Li feel unhappy or frustrated. They never thought that one was a married woman and the other was a married man, and that privately falling in love without divorcing was not allowed by law or human sentiment. They only felt that they should follow their feelings without restraint, but they didn't dare reveal the news to their husband—or wife, and didn't dare let anyone in society know. Ultimately, they were still subject to a kind of constraint. This was a latent force of the old morality commonly used in society.

▲Correction　Yesterday in "The Husband's Wife," line 17 ("was also entirely managed by Madam Li") was mistakenly printed as ("was also entirely managed by Mr. Li"). This correction is hereby made.

Social News

On Movie Sketches 204

— Lu Mengshu

(Besides those with lasting value, among Western films, I prefer the vulgar and evil ones to those that are not thorough. No matter how vulgar and absurd the "Story" is, once it is made into a movie, it gives people a wonderful Fantasy. You can treat the whole play as a beautiful dream. In a sense, movies are dreams that are slightly clearer than ordinary dreams. People not only dream when they are asleep, but also want to dream when they are awake. We go to the movie theater to have a (day dream) Day Dream, probably because of this. When I go to see movies, I always like to go during the day, and I like to go in spring and summer, especially when I have goosebumps in the spring and summer, which can best arouse various fantasies. After watching and coming back, when I sleep on the pillow at night, that kind of fantasy still comes and goes in my mind, communicating with sleep dreams. As a result, I don't know whether that is a dream or a movie. Only a beautiful phantom remains in my mind for a long time. Movies can really be called dreams made by humans using machines. The progress of science and the development of human intelligence have given us all kinds of crafts, and even dreams are made. Although wine and music are said to be the greatest masterpieces of human works, movies are indeed one of the greatest masterpieces...)

For more than ten years, I have been watching movies with a single-minded yearning, and I naturally express twelve points of sympathy for the above paragraph, and ("that kind of fantasy still comes and goes in my mind, communicating with sleep dreams") is nothing less than writing a confession for me. The above paragraph is a section from "The Artist's Home" by the modern Japanese writer Jun'ichirō Tanizaki. I transcribed it from Tian Han's ("Silver Dream"). ("Silver Dream") is a small book that I compiled from various issues of ("Silver Star") on a winter night in the 17th year of the Republic of China and handed it over to Liangyou Bookstore and Printing Company for publication. At that time, it was a severely cold night. There was neither a stove nor an electric light in the pavilion room. Only in the dim light of the flickering candlelight, in the shivering cold, I compiled it, drinking two pots of boiled water, smoking more than a dozen cigarettes, and burning two small holes in my cotton robe with the cigarettes. It is a kind of film essay, a masterpiece written in the era before the southern tour and Proletariat. The lightness and beauty of the writing, the elegance and smoothness of the writing, all demonstrate the author's cultivation in literature. In particular, the article ("Apricot Girl") can best reveal the author's charming style of writing. The author was originally a sketching master with a long-standing reputation, and also a writer in various fields in the Chinese literary world. He has always been enthusiastic about the drama movement, and the movie has also worked hard (to go to the people), but the music is too high and few harmonize, and because of the environment, he cannot reach the people. His ambition has not been fulfilled, but therefore, in his works, there is often his (unspeakable emotion) under the guise of a topic. I have always loved his works, and I have compared them to the sensual girl on Ten Family Street, and that sensual girl has almost become the idol I privately admire. However, this is only a thing of the past. Now the author has (woken up from the silver dream). Everyone is drunk and I am the only one awake(?). Perhaps he will laugh at me, who is still snoring in the (silver dream),

Page 22

However, ("Silver Dream"), this small book, will be equal to the author's ("Traces of Spring Dreams"), and will soon (disperse like the wind and clouds).

Movies are charming goblins. She and I seem to have a predestined relationship, but also seem to have deeply rooted evil. Since making a covenant with it, I have been repeatedly devastated. Although it comes from the outside world, it cannot be said that it was not given by the movie. Its bewitching seduction makes me fascinated and intoxicated, and I suffer excessive pain without knowing it. Although I have now realized it, its passionate fire still makes me infinitely nostalgic.

Since I met the movie, I have automatically served it, doing publicity, running a monthly magazine, working hard with my hands and feet, and not stopping for several years. As a result, I won a pile of debts, and both my material and spiritual well-being suffered great damage. Unfortunately, I also had a major lawsuit because of it. That was last year. Because of the continuation of the ("Movie Monthly") contract, I had a disagreement with the publisher, and because of ("The Little History of the Star"), both sides broke down emotionally in a fit of anger, so they quarreled with each other and then resorted to the court. At that time, when they were suing each other, I was suffering from a very high fever, and my mind was confused. Everything was presided over by the proxy lawyer, and my buttocks were burned by fire. In this situation of suffering from famine and illness, in the lawsuit, it seemed that I was implicitly operating the inevitable victory of suffering losses and being deceived. Originally, I was blind to the law, let alone when I was sick and injured, how could I not suffer losses and be deceived? When a paper judgment was sent by the court clerk, the amount of compensation marked on it scared me. You can find someone with a sign to fully represent you in a lawsuit, but you have to take out the money yourself to pay for the compensation. So I gritted my teeth. Although I have only paid off a quarter of it so far, this debt must be cleared sooner or later. In this way, I have to desperately exchange my waste paper for money to make up the amount to pay off this lawsuit debt. My entire fortune is just a bald pen. The output of a bald pen is really limited for a person as stupid as me, so I am still (a grateful disciple, surrounded by debts). However, although these can be said to be self-inflicted, they cannot be regarded as the devastation I suffered because of the movie. (To be continued)
